{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01LLvpA9ikANEXe6QQVgVgmB","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"OK so `fatal_signal_pending` checks if there's a SIGKILL signal pending. This should be reliable.Now, let me think about the actual issue more carefully. The RPC code at line 1620-1626 in clnt.c:\n\n```c\nif (RPC_IS_ASYNC(task) || !fatal_signal_pending(current)) {\n\ttask->tk_action = call_allocate;\n\trpc_delay(task, HZ>>4);\n\treturn;\n}\n\nrpc_exit(task, -ERESTARTSYS);\n```\n\nThis code is saying: if buffer allocation fails, then:\n- If it's an async task or there's NO fatal signal, retry the allocation\n- If it's a sync task AND there's a fatal signal, exit with ERESTARTSYS\n\nNow, the issue mentioned in the bug report: the NFS getattr is being called from `nfs_revalidate_inode`, which is called from `nfs_lookup_revalidate`. This is being called during path lookup, which is a synchronous operation.So it's likely a sync RPC task. If the buffer allocation fails and there's a SIGKILL pending, the RPC layer exits with -ERESTARTSYS.But the question is: why would there be a SIGKILL pending during a normal NFS getattr operation?One possibility: the kernel thread that's handling the RPC call has been sent a SIGKILL by the system (e.g., during shutdown or resource cleanup).\n\nBut actually, wait. Let me reconsider the code flow:\n1. User process calls autofs unmount\n2. autofs daemon unmounts the mount point\n3. This triggers NFS revalidation\n4. NFS calls getattr via RPC\n5. The RPC task is synchronous (because we're in a syscall)\n6. If buffer allocation fails, it checks for fatal signals\n7. If SIGKILL is pending, it returns -ERESTARTSYS\n\n\nThe RPC call happens in the VFS path lookup context, which is synchronous. If a fatal signal is pending when buffer allocation fails, the RPC layer bails out with -ERESTARTSYS rather than retrying. This would explain why the getattr fails during the autofs unmount sequence.\n\nThe real puzzle is understanding the timing: SIGKILL should terminate the task immediately, yet somehow the code reaches the buffer allocation failure path. There's likely a race where the signal arrives after the RPC task starts but before allocation completes. The check at line 1620 specifically looks at `fatal_signal_pending(current)` to determine whether to proceed with the allocation or fail fast.\n\nIf this RPC getattr originates from an autofs unmount context, a signal interrupting the operation would explain the -ERESTARTSYS return. The core problem emerges when NFS treats this as a permanent failure rather than a transient interruption—it invalidates the inode and triggers unmounting. The solution requires NFS to distinguish between true errors and signal-interrupted operations, either by retrying or propagating the error appropriately rather than marking the inode as stale.\n\nAlternatively, the RPC layer itself might be the culprit. When buffer allocation fails under memory pressure or signal conditions, returning -ERESTARTSYS may not be the right choice. The signal handler should manage the signal independently, and the RPC code shouldn't be making the decision to exit with ERESTARTSYS. This behavior changed between 3.14.12 and 4.1.15; (2) The NFS layer in __nfs_revalidate_inode (fs/nfs/inode.c, lines 960-970) does not handle -ERESTARTSYS specially - it treats it like any other error; (3) The same issue propagates through nfs_lookup_verify_inode and nfs_lookup_revalidate, causing the entire mount point to become invalid.\\n\\nThe fix should: (1) Handle -ERESTARTSYS specially in __nfs_revalidate_inode by not marking the inode as invalid when this restart error is encountered; (2) Alternatively, prevent the RPC layer from returning -ERESTARTSYS during buffer allocation failures, or handle buffer allocation failures differently when signals are pending; (3) Propagate restart errors appropriately to the VFS layer for proper signal handling instead of treating them as fatal inode errors.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1454,"cache_read_input_tokens":78610,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1454},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"900197f8-0274-4b80-aa99-5b9ab2cbaabc","uuid":"d13dff65-50db-43d4-bf65-d57d1dc3b6c9"}

So there are TWO places where -ERESTARTSYS can come from:\n1. In call_allocate (line 1626 in clnt.c) when buffer allocation fails and there's a fatal signal\n2. In __rpc_execute (line 783-792 in sched.c) when the sync task is waiting for the RPC to complete and a signal is received\n\nThe second path is particularly interesting. The task is waiting for the RPC to complete (waiting for the server reply), and while it's waiting, a signal is delivered. The wait function returns -ERESTARTSYS, which causes the task to exit with this error even though the reply might be in the process of being received.\n\nThis matches the bug report description: \"server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply\". The server sends the reply, but the client task is interrupted by a signal while waiting for the reply, so it exits with -ERESTARTSYS before the reply is fully processed.\n\nSo the fix should probably be: when a signal is received while waiting for an RPC reply, don't immediately exit with -ERESTARTSYS. Instead, check if the reply has already been received, and if so, process it. The issue occurs in the following sequence: (1) During autofs mount expiration, nfs_lookup_revalidate is called to validate the mount point; (2) nfs_lookup_verify_inode calls __nfs_revalidate_inode which attempts a getattr RPC call; (3) In the RPC layer's call_allocate function, if buffer allocation fails and a fatal signal is detected, the RPC task exits with -ERESTARTSYS (error -512); (4) __nfs_revalidate_inode treats this as a real error and propagates it; (5) nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns the error, causing nfs_lookup_revalidate to return 0 (invalid); (6) The dentry is invalidated, causing the autofs mount point to be unmounted.\\n\\nRoot causes: (1) The RPC layer's call_allocate (line 1620-1626 in net/sunrpc/clnt.c) returns -ERESTARTSYS when buffer allocation fails and fatal_signal_pending(current) is true. This behavior changed between 3.14.12 and 4.1.15; (2) The NFS layer in __nfs_revalidate_inode (fs/nfs/inode.c, lines 960-970) does not handle -ERESTARTSYS specially - it treats it like any other error; (3) The same issue propagates through nfs_lookup_verify_inode and nfs_lookup_revalidate, causing the entire mount point to become invalid.\\n\\nThe fix should: (1) Handle -ERESTARTSYS specially in __nfs_revalidate_inode by not marking the inode as invalid when this restart error is encountered; (2) Alternatively, prevent the RPC layer from returning -ERESTARTSYS during buffer allocation failures, or handle buffer allocation failures differently when signals are pending; (3) Propagate restart errors appropriately to the VFS layer for proper signal handling instead of treating them as fatal inode errors.\"\n}","new_string":"{\n  \"buggy_files\": [\n    \"net/sunrpc/sched.c\",\n    \"fs/nfs/inode.c\"\n  ],\n  \"buggy_functions\": [\n    \"__rpc_execute\",\n    \"__nfs_revalidate_inode\"\n  ],\n  \"confidence\": 0.8,\n  \"reasoning\": \"The bug manifests as NFS mount disappearance during autofs mount expiration. Let me create a final summary of the fault localization:\n\n## Summary\n\nI have successfully identified the root cause of the NFS mount disappearance bug during autofs mount expiration.
